Key Contributors to Jadal in Usul al-Fiqh
Survey of key scholars of jadal in usul al-fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the major scholars who advanced jadal methodology in usul al-fiqh, their key works, and their distinctive dialectical contributions.

Core Idea
Jadal in usul al-fiqh was systematically developed by both Ash'ari and Mu'tazili scholars through structured refutation and presentation.

The development of dialectical methodology (jadal) in usul al-fiqh was shaped by several prominent scholars from different theological schools. This lesson surveys four key figures: al-Baqillani (Ash'ari), Abd al-Jabbar (Mu'tazili), Abu al-Husayn (Mu'tazili), and Abu Ya'la (Hanbali). Understanding their contributions helps you see how jadal became a rigorous tool for legal theory, moving beyond mere debate into a structured method of presenting evidence and refuting opponents.

Guided Path
1
Identify al-Baqillani's role and work
Locate in the passage what al-Baqillani wrote and what his dialectical aim was. Note that his book 'al-Taqrib wa al-Irshad' was the first comprehensive usul work and that he used it to refute Mu'tazili principles.
He was an Ash'ari theologian.
2
Identify Abd al-Jabbar's role and work
Find the Mu'tazili judge's lost book 'al-'Ahd' and note how al-Zarkashi praised both him and al-Baqillani for expanding and clarifying earlier usul works.
His work is known only through later citations.
3
Examine Abu al-Husayn's methodology
Read the description of Abu al-Husayn's method in 'al-Mu'tamad'. He presented abstract rules, argued his view, and when there was disagreement, he gave opposing opinions and refuted them. This is a clear dialectical structure.
He was Abd al-Jabbar's student.
4
Note Abu Ya'la's parallel contribution
Identify Abu Ya'la al-Farra' al-Hanbali and his work 'al-'Udda', which the author says is equally important and follows a similar dialectical method. This shows the approach was used across schools.
He represents the Sunni (Hanbali) tradition.

فأكثر فيها القاضي الكلام ووسع العبارة وزاد في الإسهاب، ثم التفت إلى الحاضرين وقال : اشهدوا علي إنه إن أعاد ما قلت لا غير لم أطالبه بالجواب، أراد خصمه بذلك تعجيز . والمعروف عن الباقلاني أنه كان عالمًا من علماء الكلام على المذهب الأشعري، وكانت له صولات وجولات في الدفاع عن مذهبه العقدي، وحين توجه إلى البحث في علم أصول الفقه، انعكس ذلك على منهجه في تناوله لمسائله . لذلك كان له دور بارز في الدفع بحركة البحث الجدلي في أصول الفقه إلى الأمام بفضل كتابه «التقريب والإرشاد». هذا الكتاب الذي يعتبر أول كتاب مستوعب لجميع مباحث أصول الفقه، وتكمن أهميته في أن كل من جاء بعد الباقلاني من المتكلمين في الأصول كان عالة عليه، فالكتب التي استفادت منه لا تدخل تحت حصر، لأن كل من ألف كتابا في أصول الفقه أو العلوم الشرعية الأخرى التي لها علاقة بمباحث أصول الفقه، خاصة على طريقة المتكلمين، لابد وأن يذكر آراء القاضي الباقلاني، سواء صرح باسم الكتاب أو لم يصرح . أما وجه في الجانب الجدلي فتكمن أهمية كتاب الباقلاني هذا في أن مؤلفه قد همه فيه إلى إبطال قواعد المعتزلة التي لها علاقة بأصول الفقه، كالقول بالتحسين والتقبيح العقليين، ووجوب الأصلح على الله، وخلق العباد أفعالهم، وغيرها . والى جانب الباقلاني كان هناك الإمام القاضي عبد الجبار المعتزلي الذي عاش هو الآخر في القرن الرابع الهجري، وتوفي في القرن الخامس حوالي سنة 415 أو 416هـ . ألف عبد الجبار كتابًا في أصول الفقه سماه «العهد» ، وإذ أن هذا الكتاب مفقود ولم يصلنا، فسنكتفي في وصفه وبيان أهميته بما أورده الإمام الزركشي، الذي أبرز مكانة كل من الباقلاني وعبد الجبار في أصول الفقه، حين قال: البصري — فبينوا وأوضحوا وبسطوا وشرحوا، وجاء من بعده – أي الشافعي رحمه الله حتى جاء القاضيان ؛ قاضي السنة أبو بكر بن الطيب، وقاضي المعتزلة عبد الجبار، فوسعا العبارات وفكا الإشارات وبينا الإجمال، ورفعا الإشكال . بعد هذين العلمين، يأتي تلميذ الإمام عبد الجبار، الإمام أبو الحسين صاحب كتاب المعتمد في أصول الفقه الذي أعطى هو الآخر دفعا جديدا للمنهج الجدلي في دراسة مسائل أصول الفقه إذ أقام كتابه هذا على طريقة قويمة، حيث ابتدأه بمقدمة عرض فيها منهجه في التأليف وطريقته في ترتيب الموضوعات، ثم ابتدأ عرض هذه الموضوعات بترتيبها واحدا واحدا، وجرى خلال ذلك كله على طريقة موحدة، تقوم على عرض القواعد والمسائل الأصولية في أسلوب تقريري مجرد ثم الاستدلال لرأيه في المسألة، وإذا كانت المسألة مما احتدم فيها الخلاف فإنه يعرض الآراء التي دارت حولها ثم يستدل للرأي الذي يناصره، ويعرض أدلة الرأي أو الآراء المخالفة، ثم يكر عليها بالمناقشة والنقض . إلى جانب هذا العمل الذي قام به الإمام أبو الحسين البصري المعتزلي، نهض إمام من أهل السنة بعمل لا يقل عنه أهمية في ميدان البحث الأصولي القائم على المنهج الجدلي، ألا وهو الإمام أبو يعلى الفراء الحنبلي، مؤلف كتاب : (العدة)
The judge spoke at length in it, expanded the expression, and increased prolixity. Then he turned to the attendees and said: 'Bear witness that if he repeats what I said and no more, I will not demand an answer.' His opponent intended by that to incapacitate him. And it is known about al-Baqillani that he was a scholar of kalam on the Ash'ari school, and he had incursions and excursions in defending his doctrinal school. When he turned to research in the science of usul al-fiqh, that was reflected in his methodology in dealing with its issues. Therefore he had a prominent role in advancing the dialectical research movement in usul al-fiqh thanks to his book 'al-Taqrib wa al-Irshad'. This book is considered the first comprehensive book covering all topics of usul al-fiqh, and its importance lies in the fact that everyone who came after al-Baqillani from the mutakallimun in usul relied on him; the books that benefited from it are uncountable, because everyone who authored a book in usul al-fiqh or other religious sciences related to usul al-fiqh, especially in the manner of the mutakallimun, must mention the opinions of al-Baqillani, whether he named the book or not. As for the dialectical aspect, the importance of al-Baqillani's book lies in that the author intended in it to invalidate the principles of the Mu'tazila related to usul al-fiqh, such as the claim of rational good and evil, the obligation of the best for God, and the creation of actions by servants, and others. And alongside al-Baqillani was Imam Qadi Abd al-Jabbar al-Mu'tazili who lived in the fourth century AH and died in the fifth century around 415 or 416 AH. Abd al-Jabbar wrote a book in usul al-fiqh called 'al-'Ahd'. Since this book is lost and did not reach us, we will suffice in describing its importance with what Imam al-Zarkashi mentioned, who highlighted the status of both al-Baqillani and Abd al-Jabbar in usul al-fiqh when he said: 'al-Basri — they clarified, explained, expanded, and elaborated. And after him (meaning al-Shafi'i, may God have mercy on him) came the two judges: the judge of the Sunnah Abu Bakr ibn al-Tayyib and the judge of the Mu'tazila Abd al-Jabbar. They expanded the expressions, unlocked the indications, explained the summary, and removed the difficulty.' After these two scholars comes the student of Imam Abd al-Jabbar, Imam Abu al-Husayn, author of the book 'al-Mu'tamad fi Usul al-Fiqh', who gave a new impetus to the dialectical methodology in studying usul al-fiqh. He established his book on a sound method: he began it with an introduction presenting his methodology and his method of arranging topics. Then he began presenting these topics one by one, and throughout that all proceeded on a uniform method, based on presenting the rules and fundamental issues in an expositive abstract style, then arguing for his opinion on the issue. If the issue was one of intense disagreement, he presents the opinions that revolved around it, then argues for the opinion he supports, and presents the evidence of the opposing opinion(s), then attacks them with discussion and refutation. Alongside this work by Imam Abu al-Husayn al-Basri al-Mu'tazili, an imam of Ahl al-Sunnah undertook a work no less important in the field of usul research based on the dialectical methodology, namely Imam Abu Ya'la al-Farra' al-Hanbali, author of the book 'al-'Udda'.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage is a historical survey of the key figures who developed the dialectical methodology (jadal) in usul al-fiqh. It begins with al-Baqillani, an Ash'ari theologian, who advanced jadal through his work 'al-Taqrib wa al-Irshad'. The author emphasizes that this book was foundational, covering all usul topics and influencing every subsequent writer in the field, especially among the mutakallimun. Al-Baqillani's dialectical contribution was specifically to refute Mu'tazili principles like rational good/evil and the obligation of the best. The passage then turns to Abd al-Jabbar, a Mu'tazili judge, whose lost work 'al-'Ahd' is noted through al-Zarkashi's praise. Al-Zarkashi's quote highlights that both al-Baqillani and Abd al-Jabbar expanded and clarified the ambiguous points of earlier scholars like al-Shafi'i. Next, the author discusses Abu al-Husayn al-Basri, Abd al-Jabbar's student, who wrote 'al-Mu'tamad'. His methodology is described in detail: he used a uniform structure of presenting abstract rules, then arguing for his position, and when there was disagreement, he would present opposing views and refute them. Finally, the passage notes Abu Ya'la al-Farra' al-Hanbali's 'al-'Udda' as a parallel Sunni work using the same dialectical method. The overall message is that jadal in usul al-fiqh was a structured, argumentative approach developed by both Mu'tazili and Ash'ari/Hanbali scholars.

Key Terms
الجدل
أصول الفقه
المتكلمون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Jadal in usul al-fiqh was systematically advanced by al-Baqillani, Abd al-Jabbar, Abu al-Husayn, and Abu Ya'la through structured works that combined rule presentation, argumentation, and refutation.

Al-Juwaynī's Dialectical Method: A Step-by-Step Approach
Describes Imām al-Juwaynī's independent dialectical method in his book al-Burhān.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and sequence the key steps of Imām al-Juwaynī's dialectical method for analyzing uṣūlī principles as described in al-Burhān.

Core Idea
Al-Juwaynī divides each general rule into its specific cases and argues each separately.

Imām al-Juwaynī's al-Burhān stands as a landmark in uṣūl al-fiqh because of its unique dialectical method. Unlike his predecessors, al-Juwaynī approached each issue by first breaking it down into its constituent sub-cases, then analyzing each with logical consistency. This lesson walks you through his method step by step, showing how he combines critique of earlier views with innovation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general principle
Find the uṣūlī principle al-Juwaynī is discussing. This is the starting point of his analysis.
For example, the principle that a command implies obligation.
2
Divide into partial cases
Notice how he splits the general principle into its specific sub-issues. This allows for precise analysis.
e.g., commands may be absolute or conditional, general or specific.
3
Examine disagreements
For controversial matters, identify how he formulates a question and lists the different scholarly opinions.
He presents the issue as a question, then mentions the views of various scholars.
4
State his position
He either selects one of the existing opinions or innovates a new view based on his own reasoning.
5
Illustrate with a fiqh branch
If the principle might be confusing, he provides a concrete fiqh example to show how the difference affects the ruling.
This grounds the theoretical discussion in practical law.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لم يكن الشيرازي وحده في ميدان الدفاع عن قواعد أصول المذهب الشافعي، وإنما كان إلى جانبه عالم آخر لم يكن يقل عنه مكانة ولا قوة حجة، ذلك هو إمام الحرمين أبو المعالي عبد الملك بن عبد الله الجويني (ت: 478 هـ) الذي اشتهر في ميدان البحث الأصولي بكتابه البرهان في أصول الفقه الذي ألفه بعد نضج فكره وأصبح أحد أبرز أركان المذهب الشافعي في عصره. هذا الكتاب الذي يستمد أهميته من المنهج المستقل الذي اتخذه الجويني في تأليفه، إذ تفرد بمسلكه في تقرير القواعد الأصولية والاستدلال عليها، والقائم على نقد مسالك السابقين واستحداث مسالك جديدة محلها، وإن لم يخرج في النهاية عن المنهج الجدلي في دراسة قواعد أصول الفقه. يقوم مسلك الجويني في دراسة القواعد الأصولية على تقسيم القضايا العامة إلى صورها الجزئية، ثم يتناول كل صورة بالدراسة والتحليل على حدة، في أسلوب منطقي متسق، وفي تناوله لكل مسألة يقرر القاعدة الأصولية أولا على وفق رأيه فيها، أما إذا كانت المسألة مما احتدم حولها الخلاف فإنه يطرحها في صورة تساؤل، ثم يذكر آراء العلماء فيها، ويبين رأيه هو بعد ذلك، إما باختيار أحد الآراء أو إحداث رأي جديد وإذا رأى أن القاعدة قد تلتبس أمام الدارس ولا تكون واضحة في ذهنه جيدًا، فإنه يمثل لها بفرع فقهي، ويبين أثر الاختلاف في القاعدة في هذا الفرع الفقهي. هذا، ومن مزايا طريقة الجويني الجدلية في دراسة المسائل الأصولية؛ حرصه على ضبط المسائل وتحرير محل النزاع فيها، وكذلك استعراض أدلة المذاهب المخالفة بكل موضوعية بحيث يورد أوجه استدلالهم بها، ويردها إلى أصولها التي تضبطها، ثم يبين وجه فساد استشهادهم بها إن كان هذا الوجه مما لا يرتضيه نظره، وهو إلى ذلك حريص على دراسة المسائل الواقعية ونقد المناهج الاستدلالية الأخرى القائمة على افتراض المسائل والاعتراضات غير الواقعية. إن لهذا الكتاب أهمية بالغة بين الكتب التي درست مسائل أصول الفقه على الطريقة الجدلية، وهذه الأهمية يبرزها محققه الدكتور عبد العظيم الديب حين يقول : إذا كانت رسالة الشافعي رضي الله عنه وأرضاه تعتبر أصل الأصول، ومفتتح هذا العلم ومبدأه فإن كتاب البرهان - فيما نرى ونعلم - أول كتاب يتلوها في تاريخ علم الأصول من حيث المنزلة.
Al-Shirazi was not alone in the field of defending the principles of the Shafi'i school, but alongside him was another scholar no less in status or strength of argument: he is Imam al-Haramayn Abu al-Ma'ali 'Abd al-Malik ibn 'Abd Allah al-Juwayni (d. 478 AH), who became famous in the field of usul research for his book al-Burhan fi Usul al-Fiqh, which he authored after his thought had matured and became one of the most prominent pillars of the Shafi'i school in his time. This book derives its importance from the independent methodology that al-Juwayni adopted in its composition, for he was unique in his approach in establishing usuli principles and reasoning upon them, based on criticizing the approaches of his predecessors and innovating new approaches in their place, although ultimately he did not depart from the dialectical method in studying the principles of usul al-fiqh. Al-Juwayni's approach in studying usuli principles is based on dividing general issues into their partial cases, then studying and analyzing each case separately, in a consistent logical style. In his treatment of each issue, he first establishes the usuli principle according to his opinion on it. If the issue is one of intense disagreement, he presents it in the form of a question, then mentions the opinions of scholars on it, and then clarifies his own opinion, either by selecting one of the opinions or by creating a new opinion. If he sees that the principle might be confusing to the student and not clear in his mind, he illustrates it with a fiqh branch and clarifies the effect of the difference on the principle in that fiqh branch. Among the merits of al-Juwayni's dialectical method in studying usuli issues are his careful control of issues, defining the point of dispute, as well as objectively presenting the evidence of opposing schools, so that he mentions their points of inference and traces them back to the principles that govern them, then shows the invalidity of their citation if that aspect does not meet his approval. Moreover, he is keen to study real issues and criticize other inferential methodologies based on hypothetical issues and unrealistic objections. This book holds great significance among books that studied issues of usul al-fiqh in the dialectical manner, and this significance is highlighted by its editor Dr. 'Abd al-'Azim al-Dib when he says: If al-Shafi'i's Risala, may Allah be pleased with him, is considered the foundation of usul and the opening of this science and its beginning, then the book al-Burhan – as far as we see and know – is the first book to follow it in the history of the science of usul in terms of status.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage describes the dialectical method of Imām al-Juwaynī in his seminal work al-Burhān fī Uṣūl al-Fiqh. The author begins by positioning al-Juwaynī alongside al-Shīrāzī as a key defender of Shāfiʿī school principles, noting that al-Juwaynī's book gained importance from his independent methodology, which involved criticizing earlier approaches while remaining within the dialectical (jadal) framework. The core of his method is then explained: he first divides general legal questions into their specific sub-cases, then studies each in a logically consistent manner. For issues with scholarly disagreement, he poses a question, reviews the various opinions, and then states his own position—either adopting an existing view or innovating a new one. To clarify unclear principles, he uses practical fiqh examples (furūʿ fiqhiyya) to show how the difference affects the ruling. The passage highlights several merits: precision in defining the exact point of dispute (taḥrīr maḥall al-nizāʿ), objective presentation of opposing evidence with an analysis of their inferential foundations, and a focus on real (not hypothetical) issues. Finally, the editor's estimation is quoted, ranking al-Burhān just after al-Shāfiʿī's Risāla in importance. Throughout, the emphasis is on al-Juwaynī's systematic, analytical, and dialectical approach to uṣūl al-fiqh.

Key Terms
المنهج الجدلي
تحرير محل النزاع
صورة جزئية

Checkpoint
What does al-Juwaynī do when he encounters a principle that might be confusing to the student?
A) He ignores it.
B) He illustrates it with a fiqh branch and shows the effect of the difference.
C) He repeats the principle several times.
D) He asks the student to memorize it.

Key Takeaway
Al-Juwaynī's method systematically breaks down general uṣūlī principles into their specific sub-cases and subjects each to dialectical analysis with opposing views and concrete examples.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Take a uṣūlī principle such as 'amr (command) and its implication of obligation. Following al-Juwaynī's method, list the different sub-cases (e.g., whether the command is absolute or conditional), then state the opposing views, and finally formulate your own position with a fiqh branch example.

Key Features of al-Juwaynī's Dialectical Method: Taḥrīr and Objectivity
Describes Imām al-Juwaynī's independent dialectical method in his book al-Burhān.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe how al-Juwaynī ensures precision and objectivity in his dialectical method through taḥrīr maḥall al-nizāʿ and objective evidence presentation.

Core Idea
Al-Juwaynī defines the exact point of dispute before advancing his own argument.

Beyond the step-by-step procedure, al-Juwaynī's dialectical method is characterized by two distinctive features: precise definition of the point of disagreement (taḥrīr maḥall al-nizāʿ) and objective presentation of opposing evidence. This lesson explores these features and their importance in uṣūl al-fiqh debate.

Guided Path
1
Locate taḥrīr maḥall al-nizāʿ
Identify where al-Juwaynī clarifies exactly what the disagreement is about. This ensures focused debate.
He carefully controls the issue so that the dispute is well-defined.
2
Observe evidence presentation
See how he presents the arguments of opposing schools without bias, mentioning their points of inference.
He traces their evidence back to the principles that govern them.
3
Analyze his critique
He then shows the invalidity of their citation if it does not meet his approval, based on reasoned analysis.
4
Focus on real issues
He avoids hypothetical scenarios and criticises methodologies that rely on unrealistic objections.
This keeps the discussion grounded in practical usul.

Razi's Dialectical Method in al-Mahsul
Describes Razi's comprehensive dialectical approach in al-Mahsul.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and describe the key components of Razi's dialectical method as presented in al-Mahsul.

Core Idea
Razi systematized jadal: present rule, opposing views, evidence, and refutation.

Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi's al-Mahsul is the culmination of the dialectical method in usul al-fiqh. This lesson breaks down his systematic approach to presenting and defending usuli rules, which includes a structured sequence of stating the rule, presenting opposing views, offering evidence, and refuting objections.

Guided Path
1
Identify the foundational step
Razi begins by clearly stating the usuli rule he is addressing. Notice how he does not assume the rule is self-evident but presents it as a claim to be examined.
The rule is often introduced with 'يقرر القاعدة الأصولية'.
2
Recognize the inclusion of opposing views
After stating the rule, Razi mentions the opinion or opinions that contradict it. Sometimes he even frames the rule as a question if the topic is disputed. This ensures all sides are considered.
Look for phrases like 'ثم يأتي على ذكر الرأي أو الآراء المخالفة'.
3
Analyze the evidence presentation
Razi presents his own evidence (adilla) for his preferred view, but importantly, he anticipates objections from opponents for each piece of evidence and immediately provides answers. This shows his thoroughness.
The text mentions 'أدلة مذهبه مع اعتراضات المخالفين عن كل دليل والإجابة عن كل اعتراض'.
4
Examine the refutation of opponents
After defending his own evidence, Razi then presents the evidence of the opposing school and systematically refutes it. He uses strong language and logical reasoning to invalidate their arguments.
Observe the phrase 'نقض أدلة المخالفين'.
5
Observe the role of definitions
Throughout, Razi is careful to define usuli terms thoroughly. He not only gives a definition but explains it word-by-word, then discusses potential objections to the definition. This ensures conceptual clarity.
The passage highlights that he does not just state definitions, but explains each word and refutes objections.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أخيرًا إلى الرجل الذي أعطى للطريقة الجدلية في أصول الفقه غاية تمامها، وبلغ بها أوج غاياتها واستوفى كل المسائل الأصولية على أساسها، بنفس طويل وقدرة فائقة على المناقشة والجدل والحجاج، ذلك هو الإمام فخر صاحب كتاب (المحصول في أصول الفقه)، هذا الكتاب الذي خاتمة الكتب الرائدة في علم أصول الفقه إذ أن الذين جاؤوا بعده لم أحد أن يرقى إلى مستوى ما وصل إليه، إضافة إلى أن هذا الكتاب جمع حصيلة أهم كتب الأصول التي كتبت قبله، وذلك بأفصح أساليب التعبير وأجود طرائق الترتيب والتهذيب، مضافا إليها من آرائه وفوائد فكره وحسن إيراداته. منهج الرازي في دراسة المسائل الأصولية في هذا الكتاب، فإنه لم يحد كما ذكرنا عن الطريقة الجدلية فهو يقرر القاعدة الأصولية بناء على ما فيها، ثم يأتي على ذكر الرأي أو الآراء المخالفة، وأحيانًا يطرح القاعدة في شكل تساؤل إذا كانت مما كثر فيها الخلاف، ثم يحققها تحقيقا مفصلا يقوده إلى ترجيح أحد الآراء في شأنها وبعد عرض الآراء يأتي الرازي على ذكر أدلة مذهبه مع اعتراضات المخالفين عن كل دليل والإجابة عن كل اعتراض، ثم ذكر أدلة المخالفين ونقضها، وما يلاحظ في هذا المجال أن الرازي طويل النفس في عرض الأدلة وبيان أوجه الاستشهاد بها باستعمال اللغة وصور المنطق الكثيفة الحضور في كل صفحات الكتاب، ثم شدة الحجة وقوتها حين نقض أدلة المخالفين أو نقد الاستدلال بها وإبطالها. وكما يحرص الرازي على قوة الأدلة التي يستخدمها، يحرص كذلك على تعريف المصطلحات الأصولية وإعطائها حقها من البيان والإيضاح وهو في ذلك لا يكتفي بذكر التعريف فحسب، بل يتبعه بشرحه كلمة كلمة، ثم يبين أوجه الاعتراض عليه ويرد عليها. هذا وإن اكتفاءنا بذكر جهود هؤلاء العلماء في هذه المرحلة لا يعني أنه لم يكن هناك علماء آخرون قدموا إسهامات في البحث الأصولي على الطريقة الجدلية، فإن كتب التراجم تذكر لنا الكثير من هؤلاء، ولكن مؤلفاتهم لم تصلنا مع الأسف، فهي إما مفقودة تماما أو لا تزال مغمورة في خزائن المخطوطات
Finally, the man who gave the dialectical method in usul al-fiqh its complete perfection, and reached with it the pinnacle of its aims, and covered all usuli issues on its basis, with a long breath and surpassing ability in discussion, debate, and argumentation; that is Imam Fakhr, author of the book (al-Mahsul fi Usul al-Fiqh). This book is the culmination of pioneering books in the science of usul al-fiqh, for those who came after him did not reach the level he attained, in addition to the fact that this book collected the yield of the most important books of usul written before him, in the most eloquent styles of expression and the best methods of organization and refinement, adding to them his own opinions, intellectual benefits, and excellent points. Razi's method in studying usuli issues in this book — he did not deviate, as we mentioned, from the dialectical method: he states the usuli rule based on what it contains, then he mentions the opposing opinion or opinions, and sometimes he poses the rule in the form of a question if it is a matter of much disagreement, then he investigates it in detail leading him to prefer one opinion concerning it. After presenting the opinions, Razi mentions the evidence for his school along with the objections of the opponents to each piece of evidence and the answer to each objection, then the evidence of the opponents and its refutation. What is observed in this regard is that Razi is long-winded in presenting evidence and clarifying the aspects of citing it, using language and forms of logic heavily present in every page of the book, and then the severity and strength of his argument when refuting the evidence of the opponents or criticizing the inference and invalidating it. And just as Razi is keen on the strength of the evidence he uses, he is also keen on defining usuli terms and giving them their due of clarification and explanation, and in that he is not content with merely mentioning the definition, but follows it with a word-by-word explanation, then he shows the aspects of objection to it and responds to them. And our limitation to mentioning the efforts of these scholars in this stage does not mean that there were no other scholars who contributed to usuli research in the dialectical method; for biographical books mention many of them, but their works have not reached us, unfortunately; they are either completely lost or still buried in manuscript libraries.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed portrait of Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi's methodological approach in his monumental work 'al-Mahsul fi Usul al-Fiqh'. It begins by establishing Razi as the pinnacle of the dialectical method in usul al-fiqh, noting his exhaustive coverage of issues and his exceptional skills in debate and argumentation. The author then describes Razi's specific procedure: he first presents the usuli rule, then mentions opposing views, often framing the rule as a question when disagreement is common. He then conducts a thorough investigation leading to his preferred opinion. After laying out the views, Razi presents his own evidence along with anticipated objections and his responses, followed by the opponents' evidence and its refutation. The passage highlights Razi's meticulousness: he is 'long-winded' in presenting evidence and uses logic and language extensively. His method also includes careful definition of terms, where he provides definitions and then explains them word by word, even discussing potential objections. Finally, the author acknowledges that many other scholars contributed to this dialectical tradition, but their works are lost or inaccessible.

Razi's Approach to Defining Terms in al-Mahsul
Describes Razi's detailed treatment of definitions in al-Mahsul.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe how Razi defines and explains usuli terms in al-Mahsul, including his practice of word-by-word explanation and rebutting objections.

Core Idea
Razi defines terms word-by-word, then defends them against objections.

The passage highlights that Razi was not only focused on argumentation but also on precise definitions. He would provide a definition, then explain each word, and finally address potential criticisms. This lesson zooms in on that aspect of his methodology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition
Find where Razi offers a definition of a key term. Notice that he does not just give a brief definition; he makes it a focal point.
The passage says: 'لا يكتفي بذكر التعريف فحسب، بل يتبعه بشرحه كلمة كلمة'.
2
Unpack the word-by-word explanation
Razi explains each word in the definition separately, showing the nuance of every component. This clarifies the exact meaning and scope.
This is a rigorous approach typical of his logical training.
3
Recognize the objections and responses
After explaining the definition, Razi then mentions possible objections to it and provides responses. This ensures the definition is robust and defensible.
The text: 'ثم يبين أوجه الاعتراض عليه ويرد عليها'.
4
Appreciate the thoroughness
This method shows that for Razi, definitions are not just starting points; they are claims that need justification and defense, just like any other rule.
It reflects his pedagogical approach: teach the term, then argue for its precision.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أخيرًا إلى الرجل الذي أعطى للطريقة الجدلية في أصول الفقه غاية تمامها، وبلغ بها أوج غاياتها واستوفى كل المسائل الأصولية على أساسها، بنفس طويل وقدرة فائقة على المناقشة والجدل والحجاج، ذلك هو الإمام فخر صاحب كتاب (المحصول في أصول الفقه)، هذا الكتاب الذي خاتمة الكتب الرائدة في علم أصول الفقه إذ أن الذين جاؤوا بعده لم أحد أن يرقى إلى مستوى ما وصل إليه، إضافة إلى أن هذا الكتاب جمع حصيلة أهم كتب الأصول التي كتبت قبله، وذلك بأفصح أساليب التعبير وأجود طرائق الترتيب والتهذيب، مضافا إليها من آرائه وفوائد فكره وحسن إيراداته. منهج الرازي في دراسة المسائل الأصولية في هذا الكتاب، فإنه لم يحد كما ذكرنا عن الطريقة الجدلية فهو يقرر القاعدة الأصولية بناء على ما فيها، ثم يأتي على ذكر الرأي أو الآراء المخالفة، وأحيانًا يطرح القاعدة في شكل تساؤل إذا كانت مما كثر فيها الخلاف، ثم يحققها تحقيقا مفصلا يقوده إلى ترجيح أحد الآراء في شأنها وبعد عرض الآراء يأتي الرازي على ذكر أدلة مذهبه مع اعتراضات المخالفين عن كل دليل والإجابة عن كل اعتراض، ثم ذكر أدلة المخالفين ونقضها، وما يلاحظ في هذا المجال أن الرازي طويل النفس في عرض الأدلة وبيان أوجه الاستشهاد بها باستعمال اللغة وصور المنطق الكثيفة الحضور في كل صفحات الكتاب، ثم شدة الحجة وقوتها حين نقض أدلة المخالفين أو نقد الاستدلال بها وإبطالها. وكما يحرص الرازي على قوة الأدلة التي يستخدمها، يحرص كذلك على تعريف المصطلحات الأصولية وإعطائها حقها من البيان والإيضاح وهو في ذلك لا يكتفي بذكر التعريف فحسب، بل يتبعه بشرحه كلمة كلمة، ثم يبين أوجه الاعتراض عليه ويرد عليها. هذا وإن اكتفاءنا بذكر جهود هؤلاء العلماء في هذه المرحلة لا يعني أنه لم يكن هناك علماء آخرون قدموا إسهامات في البحث الأصولي على الطريقة الجدلية، فإن كتب التراجم تذكر لنا الكثير من هؤلاء، ولكن مؤلفاتهم لم تصلنا مع الأسف، فهي إما مفقودة تماما أو لا تزال مغمورة في خزائن المخطوطات
Finally, the man who gave the dialectical method in usul al-fiqh its complete perfection, and reached with it the pinnacle of its aims, and covered all usuli issues on its basis, with a long breath and surpassing ability in discussion, debate, and argumentation; that is Imam Fakhr, author of the book (al-Mahsul fi Usul al-Fiqh). This book is the culmination of pioneering books in the science of usul al-fiqh, for those who came after him did not reach the level he attained, in addition to the fact that this book collected the yield of the most important books of usul written before him, in the most eloquent styles of expression and the best methods of organization and refinement, adding to them his own opinions, intellectual benefits, and excellent points. Razi's method in studying usuli issues in this book — he did not deviate, as we mentioned, from the dialectical method: he states the usuli rule based on what it contains, then he mentions the opposing opinion or opinions, and sometimes he poses the rule in the form of a question if it is a matter of much disagreement, then he investigates it in detail leading him to prefer one opinion concerning it. After presenting the opinions, Razi mentions the evidence for his school along with the objections of the opponents to each piece of evidence and the answer to each objection, then the evidence of the opponents and its refutation. What is observed in this regard is that Razi is long-winded in presenting evidence and clarifying the aspects of citing it, using language and forms of logic heavily present in every page of the book, and then the severity and strength of his argument when refuting the evidence of the opponents or criticizing the inference and invalidating it. And just as Razi is keen on the strength of the evidence he uses, he is also keen on defining usuli terms and giving them their due of clarification and explanation, and in that he is not content with merely mentioning the definition, but follows it with a word-by-word explanation, then he shows the aspects of objection to it and responds to them. And our limitation to mentioning the efforts of these scholars in this stage does not mean that there were no other scholars who contributed to usuli research in the dialectical method; for biographical books mention many of them, but their works have not reached us, unfortunately; they are either completely lost or still buried in manuscript libraries.

Finally, the author acknowledges that many other scholars contributed to this dialectical tradition, but their works are lost or inaccessible.

Al-Baqillani's Pioneering Role in Theoretical Jadal
Highlights al-Baqillani's foundational contribution to the theoretical dimension of jadal in usul al-fiqh.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify al-Baqillani's dual contribution to jadal and distinguish between applied and theoretical jadal in usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
Al-Baqillani transformed jadal from a practical skill into a codified discipline.

This passage highlights the twofold contribution of al-Baqillani to jadal: not only did he practice and develop applied debate, but he also authored the first systematic treatise on the rules of jadal. Understanding this shift from practice to theory is crucial for grasping how usul al-fiqh evolved as a rigorous science.

The second section: On the theoretical field. Indeed this second stage, just as it witnessed the development and flourishing of research in applied usuli jadal, also witnessed the emergence and flourishing of authorship in usuli jadal in its theoretical form. And just as Imam Abu Bakr al-Baqillani had the priority in developing applied usuli jadal, he also had the priority in developing it in its theoretical form, for he authored the book (Sharh) Adab al-Jadal, thereby inaugurating this new stage of dialectical research in usul al-fiqh, and paving the way for those who came after him among the usulis.

Commentary
This passage introduces a new section titled 'On the theoretical field.' It explains that the second historical stage of jadal studies saw growth not only in applied jadal (the actual practice of debating usuli issues) but also in theoretical jadal (the formal study and codification of the rules of debate). The author identifies Imam Abu Bakr al-Baqillani as the pioneer of both aspects: he was instrumental in developing the applied form, and he also wrote the first theoretical work on jadal, titled 'Sharh Adab al-Jadal' (or simply 'Adab al-Jadal'). This work inaugurated the new phase of theoretical dialectical research in usul al-fiqh, providing a foundation for later scholars.

Linguistic Definition of Jadal: The Core of Dispute
Author defines the linguistic meaning of jadal and traces its etymological root to twisting a rope

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key components of the linguistic definition of jadal as given by Ibn Manzur and Ibn Ashur, distinguishing it from ordinary argument.

Core Idea
Jadal linguistically denotes stubbornness and skill in dispute, rooted in strength and firmness.

This passage opens the study of jadal by grounding it in language. Understanding this linguistic foundation is crucial before exploring its technical usage in logic and debate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sources quoted
The passage quotes Ibn Manzur from Lisan al-'Arab and Ibn Ashur. Note their definitions.
Both emphasize the element of strength.
2
Extract the core meaning
From Ibn Manzur: 'al-jadal: al-ladad fi al-khusuma wa al-qudra 'alayha' – stubbornness and ability. From Ibn Ashur: 'al-qudra 'ala al-khisam' – ability for contention.
3
Note the verbal form
Ibn Ashur explains that the verb 'jadala' is not used in the basic form; only the derived 'jadala' meaning to overcome in debate is used.
This shows jadal requires two opponents.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المطلب الثاني : المعنى اللغوي لكلمة الجدل خاصة إضافة إلى الألفاظ السابقة التي استعملت فيها مادة (ج) . د، ل)، والتي رأينا اتفاقها في إفادة معنى جامع هو القوة والشدة والإحكام في الأمر، يأتي اللفظ الذي يهمنا في سياق البحث، وهو كلمة «الجدل بفتح الجيم والدال، وفي تعريفه لغة، قال ابن منظور : الجدل: اللدد في الخصومة والقدرة عليها، وقد جادله مجادلة وجدالا، ورجل جدل ومجدل ومجدال ؛ شديد الجدل، ويقال : جادلت الرجل فجدلته جدلا، أي غلبته، ورجل جدل إذا كان أقوى في الخصام، وجادله، أي خاصمه، مجادلة وجدالا ، والاسم الجدل وهو شدة الخصومة» وقال ابن عاشور : و المجادلة، مفاعلة من الجدل، وهو القدرة على الخصام والحجة فيه، وهي منازعة بالقول لإقناع الغير برأيك ... ولم يسمع للجدل فرع مجرد أصلي، والمسموع جادل، لأن الخصام يستدعي خصمين، وأما قولهم: جدله، فهو بمعنى غلبه في المجادلة، فليس فعلا أصليا في الاشتقاق. ومصدر المجادلة الجدال، قال تعالى: و... ولا جدال في الحجة ومنه قول الشاعر : إذا اجتمعوا على ألف وياء وتاء، هاج بينهم جدال هذا وقد اختلف في أصل اشتقاق هذا المعنى لكلمة الجدل : فقال الراغب الأصفهاني «الجدال هو المفاوضة على سبيل المنازعة ،والمغالبة، وأصله من جدلت الحبل إذا أحكمت فتله . فكأن المتجادلين يفتل كل واحد الآخر عن رأيه». وهذا الرأي يؤيده الإمام الطبرسي إذ يقول : وأصل المجادلة من الجدل وهو شدة الفتل ورجل مجدول كأنه قد جدل، أي قتل كما يؤيده أيضًا الإمام فخر الدين الرازي ، وذلك إذ يقول : الجدال، هو فعال من المجادلة، وأصله من الجدل الذي من الفتل، يقال: زمام مجدول وجديل، أي مفتول، والجديل اسم الزمام لأنه لا يكون إلا مفتولا، وسميت المخاصمة مجادلة لأن كل واحد من الخصمين يروم أن يفتل
The second sub-topic: the linguistic meaning of the word 'jadal' specifically. In addition to the previous words that used the root (j-d-l), which we have seen agree in conveying a comprehensive meaning of strength, intensity, and firmness in a matter, comes the word of interest in this research context, which is the word 'al-jadal' with the kasra on the jim and the dal. Regarding its linguistic definition, Ibn Manzur said: 'Al-jadal: stubbornness in dispute and the ability for it. And he has debated him with debate and disputation, and a man is jadl, mijdal, and mijdal: intense in debate. And it is said: I debated the man and debated him, i.e., I overcame him. And a man is jadl if he is stronger in contention. And he debated him, i.e., he disputed with him, with debate and disputation. And the noun is al-jadal, which is the intensity of dispute.' And Ibn Ashur said: 'Al-mujadala is a mutual interaction form from al-jadal, which is the ability for contention and argument therein. It is a verbal contest to convince the other of your opinion... And there is no heard verbal form of jadal as a basic triliteral, and what is heard is jādala, because contention requires two opponents. As for their saying: jadalahu, it means he overcame him in debate, so it is not a basic verb in derivation. And the verbal noun of al-mujadala is al-jidāl. Allah said: '...and no dispute in the Hajj.' And from it is the poet's saying: When they gather over alif and ya and ta, dispute arises among them.' Here, there is disagreement about the original derivation of this meaning of the word 'jadal'. Al-Raghib al-Isfahani said: 'Al-jidāl is mutual negotiation on the basis of contention and overwhelming, and its origin is from jadalta al-habl if you twisted it strongly. So it is as if the two disputants twist each other from his opinion.' This view is supported by Imam al-Tabrisi, he says: 'And the origin of al-mujadala is from al-jadl, which is intense twisting, and a man is majdūl as if he has been twisted, i.e., killed.' It is also supported by Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi, he says: 'Al-jidāl is a verbal noun from al-mujadala, and its origin is from al-jadl which is from twisting. It is said: a twisted reins and jadīl, i.e., twisted. And al-jadīl is the name for the reins because they are only twisted. And the dispute is called mujadala because each of the two opponents seeks to twist.'
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage defines the linguistic meaning of 'jadal' (dialectic) and its etymological root. The author begins by stating that this word, alongside others from the same root (j-d-l), shares a core meaning of strength and firmness. He then quotes Ibn Manzur, who defines jadal as stubbornness and ability in dispute, with derivatives indicating a person skilled in debate. The verb 'jadalahu' means he overcame him in debate. Next, Ibn Ashur explains that 'mujadalah' is a mutual interaction form, implying two opponents, and that the basic triliteral verb is not used; rather, the derived form 'jādala' is used. He cites the Quranic verse 'wa la jidala fi al-hajj' and a poetic line as examples. The passage then delves into the disagreement about the word's etymology: al-Raghib al-Isfahani traces it to 'jadalta al-habl' meaning twisting a rope strongly, so disputants figuratively 'twist' each other from their opinions. al-Tabrisi and Fakhr al-Din al-Razi support this, with al-Razi adding that dispute is called mujadala because each opponent tries to 'twist' the other. This etymological analysis highlights the logical dimension: dialectical argument is not mere shouting but a structured, forceful exchange aimed at refuting the opponent, akin to physical twisting. Throughout, the passage uses only examples from Arabic linguistics and the Islamic tradition (the Quran and poetry), consistent with the Islamic sciences rule.

Key Terms
الجدل
المجادلة

B) Stubbornness and ability in dispute

Key Takeaway
Jadal, linguistically, is not just any argument but a skilled, forceful contention rooted in strength and firmness.

The Etymological Root of Jadal: From Twisting a Rope to Twisting an Argument
Author traces the etymological root of jadal to twisting a rope.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the metaphorical link between twisting a rope (jadalta al-habl) and the dialectical process as understood by al-Raghib, al-Tabrisi, and al-Razi.

Core Idea
Jadal originates from twisting a rope, highlighting the competitive 'twisting' of each other's viewpoints.

This passage moves from definition to etymology. The root metaphor of twisting a rope reveals how jadal is a mutual struggle to 'twist' the opponent from their position, a key insight for understanding the dynamics of debate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the etymologists
Al-Raghib al-Isfahani, al-Tabrisi, and Fakhr al-Din al-Razi are cited. They all trace the word to 'jadalta al-habl'.
2
Understand the metaphor
Al-Raghib says disputants 'twist each other from his opinion'. Al-Razi says each opponent 'seeks to twist'.
The twisting is forceful, not gentle.
3
Connect to the conceptual meaning
This shows jadal involves a struggle where each party tries to overpower the other's viewpoint, not just exchange ideas.

المطلب الثاني : المعنى اللغوي لكلمة الجدل خاصة إضافة إلى الألفاظ السابقة التي استعملت فيها مادة (ج) . د، ل)، والتي رأينا اتفاقها في إفادة معنى جامع هو القوة والشدة والإحكام في الأمر، يأتي اللفظ الذي يهمنا في سياق البحث، وهو كلمة «الجدل بفتح الجيم والدال، وفي تعريفه لغة، قال ابن منظور : الجدل: اللدد في الخصومة والقدرة عليها، وقد جادله مجادلة وجدالا، ورجل جدل ومجدل ومجدال ؛ شديد الجدل، ويقال : جادلت الرجل فجدلته جدلا، أي غلبته، ورجل جدل إذا كان أقوى في الخصام، وجادله، أي خاصمه، مجادلة وجدالا ، والاسم الجدل وهو شدة الخصومة» وقال ابن عاشور : و المجادلة، مفاعلة من الجدل، وهو القدرة على الخصام والحجة فيه، وهي منازعة بالقول لإقناع الغير برأيك ... ولم يسمع للجدل فرع مجرد أصلي، والمسموع جادل، لأن الخصام يستدعي خصمين، وأما قولهم: جدله، فهو بمعنى غلبه في المجادلة، فليس فعلا أصليا في الاشتقاق. ومصدر المجادلة الجدال، قال تعالى: و... ولا جدال في الحجة ومنه قول الشاعر : إذا اجتمعوا على ألف وياء وتاء، هاج بينهم جدال هذا وقد اختلف في أصل اشتقاق هذا المعنى لكلمة الجدل : فقال الراغب الأصفهاني «الجدال هو المفاوضة على سبيل المنازعة ،والمغالبة، وأصله من جدلت الحبل إذا أحكمت فتله . فكأن المتجادلين يفتل كل واحد الآخر عن رأيه». وهذا الرأي يؤيده الإمام الطبرسي إذ يقول : وأصل المجادلة من الجدل وهو شدة الفتل ورجل مجدول كأنه قد جدل، أي قتل كما يؤيده أيضًا الإمام فخر الدين الرازي ، وذلك إذ يقول : الجدال، هو فعال من المجادلة، وأصله من الجدل الذي من الفتل، يقال: زمام مجدول وجديل، أي مفتول، والجديل اسم الزمام لأنه لا يكون إلا مفتولا، وسميت المخاصمة مجادلة لأن كل واحد من الخصمين يروم أن يفتل
The second sub-topic: the linguistic meaning of the word 'jadal' specifically. In addition to the previous words that used the root (j-d-l), which we have seen agree in conveying a comprehensive meaning of strength, intensity, and firmness in a matter, comes the word of interest in this research context, which is the word 'al-jadal' with the kasra on the jim and the dal. Regarding its linguistic definition, Ibn Manzur said: 'Al-jadal: stubbornness in dispute and the ability for it. And he has debated him with debate and disputation, and a man is jadl, mijdal, and mijdal: intense in debate. And it is said: I debated the man and debated him, i.e., I overcame him. And a man is jadl if he is stronger in contention. And he debated him, i.e., he disputed with him, with debate and disputation. And the noun is al-jadal, which is the intensity of dispute.' And Ibn Ashur said: 'Al-mujadala is a mutual interaction form from al-jadal, which is the ability for contention and argument therein. It is a verbal contest to convince the other of your opinion... And there is no heard verbal form of jadal as a basic triliteral, and what is heard is jādala, because contention requires two opponents. As for their saying: jadalahu, it means he overcame him in debate, so it is not a basic verb in derivation. And the verbal noun of al-mujadala is al-jidāl. Allah said: '...and no dispute in the Hajj.' And from it is the poet's saying: When they gather over alif and ya and ta, dispute arises among them.' Here, there is disagreement about the original derivation of this meaning of the word 'jadal'. Al-Raghib al-Isfahani said: 'Al-jidāl is mutual negotiation on the basis of contention and overwhelming, and its origin is from jadalta al-habl if you twisted it strongly. So it is as if the two disputants twist each other from his opinion.' This view is supported by Imam al-Tabrisi, he says: 'And the origin of al-mujadala is from al-jadl, which is intense twisting, and a man is majdūl as if he has been twisted, i.e., killed.' It is also supported by Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi, he says: 'Al-jidāl is a verbal noun from al-mujadala, and its origin is from al-jadl which is from twisting. It is said: a twisted reins and jadīl, i.e., twisted. And al-jadīl is the name for the reins because they are only twisted. And the dispute is called mujadala because each of the two opponents seeks to twist.'
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage defines the linguistic meaning of 'jadal' (dialectic) and its etymological root. The author begins by stating that this word, alongside others from the same root (j-d-l), shares a core meaning of strength and firmness. He then quotes Ibn Manzur, who defines jadal as stubbornness and ability in dispute, with derivatives indicating a person skilled in debate. The verb 'jadalahu' means he overcame him in debate. Next, Ibn Ashur explains that 'mujadalah' is a mutual interaction form, implying two opponents, and that the basic triliteral verb is not used; rather, the derived form 'jādala' is used. He cites the Quranic verse 'wa la jidala fi al-hajj' and a poetic line as examples. The passage then delves into the disagreement about the word's etymology: al-Raghib al-Isfahani traces it to 'jadalta al-habl' meaning twisting a rope strongly, so disputants figuratively 'twist' each other from their opinions. al-Tabrisi and Fakhr al-Din al-Razi support this, with al-Razi adding that dispute is called mujadala because each opponent tries to 'twist' the other. This etymological analysis highlights the logical dimension: dialectical argument is not mere shouting but a structured, forceful exchange aimed at refuting the opponent, akin to physical twisting. Throughout, the passage uses only examples from Arabic linguistics and the Islamic tradition (the Quran and poetry), consistent with the Islamic sciences rule.

Dialectic -- Jadal
beginner
5 min
Etymological roots of jadal: twisting vs wrestling
Examines two competing etymologies for the word jadal (dialectic).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the two proposed etymological origins of jadal (twisting vs wrestling) and explain how each metaphor shapes the conceptual understanding of dialectical argument.

Core Idea
Jadal is either twisting opinions or wrestling opponents to the ground — the metaphor you choose shapes your theory of debate.

This passage investigates the word 'jadal' (dialectic) by tracing its roots to two vivid physical actions: twisting a rope and wrestling on the ground. These metaphors reveal how classical scholars viewed dialectical argument not as polite discussion, but as a struggle of opinions—either to turn an opponent from his view or to defeat him entirely. Understanding this etymology is essential for grasping the technical term 'jadal' as used in usul al-fiqh and kalam.

Guided Path
1
Locate the two competing etymologies
Scan the Arabic passage for the two proposed origins: one from 'jadaltu al-habl' (twisting a rope) and the other from 'al-sar' 'ala al-jadala' (wrestling on the ground). Mark the key phrases that introduce each view.
The first appears after 'فقال الراغب الأصفهاني'; the second after 'وقيل'.
2
Identify the scholars supporting each etymology
List the authorities: al-Raghib, al-Tabrisi, al-Razi, and al-Zajjaj support the twisting view; Ibn 'Ashur supports the wrestling view; al-Baghawi combines both. Note how each scholar adds nuance—al-Razi provides linguistic evidence ('zimam majdul'), while Ibn 'Ashur connects 'jadala' to the ground (al-jadala).
Al-Baghawi's summary is key: he presents both views as complementary rather than contradictory.
3
Analyze the metaphorical implications
Consider the difference: if jadal is like twisting a rope, the disputant aims to 'twist' the opponent's opinion, implying persuasion and careful manipulation. If it is like wrestling, the aim is to throw the opponent down, implying domination and victory. How do these metaphors frame the purpose and method of dialectic?
The twisting metaphor aligns with sifting arguments; the wrestling metaphor emphasizes defeating the opponent.
4
Assess how al-Baghawi synthesizes both views
Read al-Baghawi's statement: he says jadal includes both 'shiddat al-mukhasama' (intense argument) and the desire to 'qahr' (overpower). This synthesis suggests that the technical term jadal in Islamic logic can encompass both subtle argumentation and forceful refutation.
This expansion shows that jadal is not a single method but a spectrum of argumentative practices.
5
Relate the etymology to the technical usage in Islamic sciences
Connect the etymology to how jadal functions in usul al-fiqh and kalam: as one of the five logical arts (al-sana'i' al-khams), jadal uses premises that are generally accepted (mashhurat) to persuade. The physical metaphors reinforce its nature as a vigorous, engaged form of reasoning.
The shift from physical struggle to intellectual combat is a key conceptual leap for the student.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الجدل
ومنه قول الشاعر : إذا اجتمعوا على ألف وياء وتاء، هاج بينهم جدال
هذا وقد اختلف في أصل اشتقاق هذا المعنى لكلمة الجدل :
فقال الراغب الأصفهاني : «الجدال هو المفاوضة على سبيل المنازعة والمغالبة، وأصله من جدلت الحبل إذا أحكمت فتله. فكأن المتجادلين يفتل كل واحد الآخر عن رأيه». وهذا الرأي يؤيده الإمام الطبرسي إذ يقول : وأصل المجادلة من الجدل وهو شدة الفتل ورجل مجدول كأنه قد جدل، أي قتل. كما يؤيده أيضًا الإمام فخر الدين الرازي ، وذلك إذ يقول : الجدال، هو فعال من المجادلة، وأصله من الجدل الذي من الفتل، يقال: زمام مجدول وجديل، أي مفتول، والجديل اسم الزمام لأنه لا يكون إلا مفتولا، وسميت المخاصمة مجادلة لأن كل واحد من الخصمين يروم أن يفتل صاحبه عن رأيه.
والعلامة الزجاج هو القائل بهذا الرأي من بين علماء اللغة العربية، كما يشير إلى ذلك الإمام فخر الدين الرازي :
وقيل : أصل الجدال، الصراع لإسقاط الإنسان صاحبه على الجدالة. قال ابن عاشور مؤكدا هذا الرأي: «وأما الجدل بفتحتين - فهو اسم المصدر، وأصله مشتق من الجدل، وهو الصرع على الأرض، لأن الأرض تسمى الجدالة - بفتح الجيم - يقال : جدله، فهو مجدول».
وقد لخص الإمام البغوي هذين الرأيين فقال : «الجدال : شدة المخاصمة من الجدل، وهو شدة الفتل، فهو يريد فتل الخصم عن مذهبه بطريق الحجاج ، وقيل : الجدال من الجدالة، وهي الأرض، فكان كل واحد من الخصمين يروم قهر صاحبه وصرعه على الجدالة». فنحن إذا اعتبرنا تسمية المنازعة الكلامية جدلا استنادًا على المعنى الأصلي
Dialectic. And among it is the saying of the poet: 'When they gather upon Alif and Ya and Ta, argument breaks out among them.' This [topic] has differed regarding the origin of the derivation of this meaning of the word 'jadal'. Al-Raghib al-Isfahani said: 'Al-jidal is discussion by way of dispute and overcoming, and its origin is from 'jadaltu al-habl' when you tightly twisted it. So it is as if the two disputants each twist the other from his opinion.' And this view is supported by Imam al-Tabrisi when he says: 'The origin of al-mujadala is from al-jadl, which is intense twisting, and a man is majdul as if he has been twisted, i.e., killed.' It is also supported by Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi when he says: 'Al-jidal is a verbal noun from al-mujadala, and its origin is from al-jadl which is from twisting. It is said: zimam majdul and jadil, i.e., twisted, and al-jadil is the name for the rein because it is only twisted. And the dispute is called mujadala because each of the two opponents intends to twist his companion from his opinion.' And al-Zajjaj is the one who holds this view among the Arabic language scholars, as indicated by Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi. And it was said: 'The origin of al-jidal is wrestling to throw one's opponent onto the ground (al-jadala).' Ibn Ashur said, confirming this view: 'As for al-jadl with two fatha: it is the verbal noun, and its origin is derived from al-jadl which is throwing onto the ground, because the ground is called al-jadala with a fatha on the jim. It is said: jadalahu, he threw him down, so he is majdul.' And Imam al-Baghawi summarized these two views and said: 'Al-jidal is intense disputation from al-jadl, which is intense twisting, so he intends to twist the opponent from his school of thought by way of argumentation. And it is said: al-jidal is from al-jadala, which is the ground, so each of the two opponents intends to overpower his companion and throw him onto the ground.' Therefore, if we consider the naming of verbal dispute as jadal based on the original meaning...
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage is a lexical and conceptual investigation into the word 'jadal' (dialectic). The author begins by citing a poetic example where letters are used metaphorically to describe argument. Then he states that scholars differ on the derivation. The first opinion, supported by al-Raghib al-Isfahani, al-Tabrisi, and Fakhr al-Din al-Razi, traces the word to 'jadl' meaning 'twisting' — as in twisting a rope. The idea is that disputants seek to twist each other's opinions, i.e., to turn them away from their position. The second opinion, attributed to al-Zajjaj and explained by Ibn 'Ashur, derives it from 'jadl' meaning 'throwing down onto the ground' (jadala). Here, disputation is seen as a kind of wrestling where each aims to overthrow the opponent. Finally, Imam al-Baghawi combines both views, showing that the term encompasses both 'intense twisting' (shiddat al-fatl) and 'wrestling on the ground'. The author concludes by noting that the naming of verbal dispute as jadal can be based on either original meaning, implying a synthesis. The passage thus establishes the semantic range of the term, linking it to both verbal manipulation and physical contest.

Key Takeaway
The word jadal derives from either rope-twisting or ground-wrestling, metaphors that shape its technical meaning in Islamic dialectic.

The Linguistic Roots of Jadal
Author examines multiple proposed etymologies of the word 'jadal' from Arabic linguistics.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three proposed etymologies of the term 'jadal' and explain how each root meaning informs the concept of dialectical debate in Islam.

Core Idea
Jadal is rooted in physical struggle—twisting ropes and throwing opponents to the ground—revealing debate as intellectual combat.

The term 'jadal' is central to Islamic dialectics, but its linguistic origins are often overlooked. In this passage, classical scholars trace the word to three distinct roots: twisting strength, throwing to the ground, and even unripe dates. Understanding these roots illuminates why Islamic debate is framed as a high-stakes, rigorous intellectual contest.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three proposed roots
Look for the three distinct Arabic words from which 'jadal' is said to be derived: al-jadl (twisting/strength), al-jadalah (earth/ground), and al-jidal (unripe dates).
Each root is supported by different scholars.
2
Understand the conceptual link for each root
For each root, see how the commentator connects the physical action (twisting a rope, throwing to the ground) to the activity of debate. For example, twisting a rope symbolizes strengthening an argument, while throwing to the ground symbolizes overpowering an opponent.
This helps explain why jadal is not mere quarreling.
3
Trace the scholarly authorities cited
Note which scholars support each derivation: al-Zajjaj and Ibn Ashur for jadalah, al-Baghawi for both jadl and jadalah, al-Tufi for all three including the date reference.
Al-Tufi's view is the most comprehensive.
4
Synthesize the overall understanding of jadal
Conclude that jadal is not mere argument but a disciplined, forceful, and sometimes combative exchange aimed at establishing truth. The linguistic roots emphasize strength, grounding, and even the ripeness of arguments.
This synthesis will help you appreciate the term's depth in Islamic scholarship.

صاحبه عن رأيه (1) . (2) والعلامة الزجاج هو القائل بهذا الرأي من بين علماء اللغة العربية، كما يشير إلى ذلك الإمام فخر الدين الرازي : وقيل : أصل الجدال، الصراع لإسقاط الإنسان صاحبه على الجدالة»(3) قال ابن عاشور مؤكدا هذا الرأي: «وأما الجدل بفتحتين - فهو اسم المصدر، وأصله مشتق من الجدل، وهو الصرع على الأرض، لأن الأرض تسمى الجدالة - بفتح الجيم . بفتح الجيم - يقال : جدله . يقال : جدله، فهو مجدول» (4) (5) هذين الرأيين فقال : وقد لخص الإمام البغوي ، «الجدال : شدة المخاصمة من الجدل، وهو شدة الفتل، فهو يريد فتل الخصم عن مذهبه بطريق الحجاج ، وقيل : الجدال من الجدالة، وهي الأرض، فكان كل واحد من الخصمين يروم قهر صاحبه وصرعه على الجدالة» (6) . فنحن إذا اعتبرنا تسمية المنازعة الكلامية جدلا استنادًا على المعنى الأصلي الأول، فذلك لأن كل واحد من المتجادلين يحرص على التمسك برأيه ويعمل على تقويته وإحكامه بما يقدمه من أدلة وحجج وبما يكشفه من وهن في رأي خصمه وأدلته . . وإذا اعتبرنا التسمية متأتية عن المعنى الأصلي الثاني، فذلك لأن كل واحد من المتجادلين إنما يجتهد في استجماع قواه العقلية والخطابية بإبراز المقدمات لمم إظهار الشواهد لتأكيد وجاهة ما التزم به من مذهب وما اعتنقه من مبدأ، قصد تبكيت خصمه ومباهتته (1) ، فكأن كل واحد من الخصمين يقاوم صاحبه حتى يغلبه فيكون كمن ضرب به الجدالة ( 2 ) . والذي يراه الطوفي رحمه الله أن لفظ «الجدل « يمكن اشتقاقه من كل المعاني السابقة، إذ يقول: (3) «أما اشتقاق الجدل فيتجه من أصول بناء على ما عرف في علم الاشتقاق أنه متى اتفق اللفظان في المعنى والحروف الأصول، جاز الاشتقاق . . . فيمكن اشتقاق الجدل من الجدل بسكون الدال وهو الشد والإحكام، يقال: جدلت الحبل أجدله جدلا كتصريف فتلته أفتله فتلا إذا فتلته فتلا شديدًا محكما، ومنه جارية مجدولة الخلق أي محكمة البنية والأجدل ،الصقر، لاشتداد خلقته وقوته ، في نفسه، ولا شك أن في الجدل معنى الشد والإحكام، لأن كلا من الخصمين يشتد على خصمه ويضايقه بالحجة التي اجتهد في إحكامها. ويمكن اشتقاقه من الجدالة - بفتح الجيم وهي الأرض، كأن كل واحد من المتجادلين يقصد غلبة صاحبه وصرعه في مقام النطق كما يجدل الفارس قرنه، أي يرميه بالجدالة ، يقال : طعنه فجدله وانجدل هو إذا سقط . ويمكن اشتقاقه من الجدال - بفتح الجيم وبغير هاء، وهو البلح إذا اخضر واستدار قبل اشتداده بلغة أهل نجد، كأن كل واحد من المتجادلين يقصد
His companion from his opinion (1). (2) And the scholar al-Zajjaj is the one who holds this opinion among the scholars of the Arabic language, as indicated by Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi: And it was said: The origin of jidal (debate) is the struggle to throw a person, his companion, onto the ground (jadala). (3) Ibn Ashur said, affirming this opinion: 'As for al-jadal with two fathas [i.e., jadal] — it is a verbal noun, and its origin is derived from al-jadl, which is throwing onto the ground, because the ground is called al-jadalah — with a fatha on the jim. With a fatha on the jim — it is said: jadalahu [he threw him]. It is said: jadalahu, so he is majdul [thrown].' (4) (5) These two opinions, then he said: And Imam al-Baghawi summarized: 'Al-jidal is the intensity of contention from al-jadl, which is intense twisting; so he intends to twist the opponent away from his doctrine through the method of argumentation. And it is said: al-jidal is from al-jadalah, which is the earth, so each of the two opponents seeks to overpower his companion and throw him onto the earth.' (6) So if we consider the naming of verbal dispute as jadal based on the first original meaning, then that is because each of the two disputants is keen to hold onto his opinion and works to strengthen and tighten it by what he presents of proofs and arguments and by uncovering the weakness in his opponent's opinion and arguments... And if we consider the naming as derived from the second original meaning, then that is because each of the two disputants strives to gather his intellectual and rhetorical powers by presenting premises and bringing forth evidences to affirm the validity of what he has committed to of doctrine and what he has embraced of principle, aiming to silence his opponent and refute him (1), so it is as if each of the two opponents resists his companion until he overcomes him, like one who is struck with the jadalah (2). And what al-Tufi, may Allah have mercy on him, holds is that the word 'jadal' can be derived from all of the previous meanings, as he says: (3) 'As for the derivation of jadal, it is possible from origins based on what is known in the science of derivation: whenever two words agree in meaning and original letters, derivation is permissible... So it is possible to derive jadal from al-jadl with a sukun on the dal, which is strength and tightness. It is said: jadaltu al-habla a judluhu jadlan (I twisted the rope strongly and tightly), just like fataftuhu aftuluhu fatlan if you twisted it tightly and strongly. From this is jarid ma jadulat al-khalq (a girl with a strong and well-built body), and al-ajdal (the falcon) due to the strength of its constitution and its power in itself. And there is no doubt that in jadal there is the meaning of strength and tightness, because each of the two opponents exerts strength against his opponent and harasses him with the argument he has striven to strengthen. And it can be derived from al-jadalah — with a fatha on the jim — which is the earth; it is as if each of the two disputants intends to overcome his companion and throw him down in the arena of speech, just as the horseman throws his opponent, i.e., he hurls him onto the jadalah. It is said: ta'anahu fa jadalahu wa injadala huwa idha saqata (he stabbed him and threw him down, and he fell down). And it can be derived from al-jidal — with a fatha on the jim and without a ha — which is unripe dates when they become green and round before ripening, in the dialect of the people of Najd; it is as if each of the two disputants intends...
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage is a linguistic investigation into the etymology of the term 'jadal' (dialectics) as used in Islamic logic and argumentation theory. The author begins by noting that al-Zajjaj (a grammarian and exegete) is among those who trace 'jadal' to the root meaning of throwing a person to the ground (jadalah). This view is also supported by Ibn Ashur, who explicitly states that 'jadal' (with two fathas) is a verbal noun derived from 'jadl', meaning to hurl someone to the earth, thus linking verbal debate to physical struggle. The author then mentions Imam al-Baghawi's summary, which encompasses two interpretations: one from 'jadl' meaning intense twisting (of a rope or argument), and another from 'jadalah' meaning ground. Al-Baghawi explains that a debater aims to twist his opponent away from his position through argumentation, or to throw him onto the ground figuratively. The passage then elaborates on how these two meanings apply to actual disputation: if the term is based on the first meaning (strength and twisting), each debater holds fast to his view and strengthens it with proofs, while exposing weaknesses in the opponent's case. If derived from the second meaning (throwing to the ground), each debater marshals all his mental and rhetorical resources to display evidences and uphold his doctrine, aiming to silence and overwhelm the opponent, like one who physically throws another onto the earth. The passage concludes with the view of al-Tufi, who argues that all these meanings are valid derivations, citing principles of Arabic etymology. He provides detailed analogies: from 'jadl' (twisting a rope strongly) to describe well-built objects and the falcon's strength; from 'jadalah' (earth) to the act of throwing; and even from 'jidal' (unripe dates) to symbolize the premature or incomplete state of argumentation, suggesting that debaters sometimes aim to strike at an opponent before arguments fully mature. The passage thus establishes the rich semantic field of 'jadal', emphasizing that it encompasses both physical struggle and intellectual contest.

Key Terms
الجدل
الجدالة
الجدال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) From 'jadalah' meaning earth or ground

D) From 'jadal' meaning a form of poetry

Key Takeaway
The term 'jadal' in Islamic logic is linguistically rooted in physical combat, reflecting the intense, disciplined effort required in scholarly debate.

Analyzing al-Baji's Definition of Jadal
Author presents al-Baji's definition of jadal and offers two criticisms.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the components of al-Baji's definition of jadal and evaluate its two criticisms.

Core Idea
A definition can be too broad and too narrow at the same time.

In this lesson, we examine the definition of jadal (dialectic) by the Maliki scholar al-Baji. He defines jadal as an exchange of speech between two people each aiming to correct his own statement and refute the other's. Our author raises two key criticisms: the definition is too general, covering all fields, and too restrictive, requiring two participants. Let's break down these points.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum and definiens
Find the term being defined (jadal) and the defining phrase. Al-Baji says it is 'the exchange of speech between two, each one intending to correct his own statement and invalidate the statement of his companion.'
2
Extract the genus and differentia
The genus is 'exchange of speech' (verbal interaction). The differentia includes two restrictions: (1) between two persons, and (2) each has the intention of correcting himself and refuting the other.
This is a definition by genus and differentia, though not formalized as such.
3
Analyze the first criticism: over-generality
The author notes that the definition is not specific to any scientific field; it would apply to any verbal exchange with those intentions, from theology to mundane arguments. This makes it too broad.
A good definition should be specific to the subject matter.
4
Analyze the second criticism: restriction to two participants
Al-Baji's definition limits jadal to two people. The author argues that one can engage in jadal alone by mentally simulating an opponent's objections and answering them, as legal theorists do in their writings.
This shows the definition is too narrow, excluding solitary dialectical reasoning.
5
Consider the alternative: solitary jadal
The author presents solitary jadal as a valid form, where a scholar examines his own opinion, anticipates counterarguments, and responds, exhausting all possibilities. This is common in usul al-fiqh works.
This critique expands the concept of jadal beyond face-to-face debate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
3 - تعريف الباجي (ت: 474 هـ) : عرف الإمام أبو الوليد الباجي (1) الجدل بأنه : تردد الكلام بين اثنين قصد كل واحد منهما تصحيح قوله وإبطال قول صاحبه»(2). هذا التعريف يمكن أن نلاحظ عليه هو الآخر ما يلي: — أنه كذلك تعريف عام لا يتعلق بمجال علمي معين، وإنما يمتد ليغطي المجالات العلمية كلها . - أنه يقصر الجدل على ما يدور بين اثنين فقط، في حين أنه يمكن أن يديره الواحد لوحده، وذلك بأن يقرر رأيه في مسألة من المسائل، ثم يستحضر رأي من يخالفه فيها، ويدير معه حوارًا حول الاحتمالات التي يمكن أن يطرحها، ويجيب عنها الواحدة بعد الأخرى، بحيث يستفرغ كافة الفروض العقلية الممكنة، كما يجري عليه حال الأصوليين في مؤلفاتهم الأصولية.
3 - Definition of al-Baji (d. 474 AH): Imam Abu al-Walid al-Baji defined jadal as: 'The exchange of speech between two, each one intending to correct his own statement and invalidate the statement of his companion.' This definition - also - we note the following about it: - That it is likewise a general definition not related to a specific scientific field, rather it extends to cover all scientific fields. - That it restricts jadal to what occurs between two only, whereas one can conduct it by himself, such that he determines his opinion on a matter, then brings to mind the opinion of one who opposes him in it, and conducts with him a dialogue regarding the possibilities that can be raised, and answers them one after another, such that he exhausts all possible rational assumptions, as is the practice of legal theorists in their works on legal theory.
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage presents the definition of jadal (dialectic) by the Maliki scholar Abu al-Walid al-Baji (d. 474 AH/1081 CE) and then critiques it. Al-Baji defines jadal as an exchange of speech between two individuals, each aiming to correct his own position and refute the other's. The author then raises two criticisms. First, the definition is overly general, applying to any field and not specific to any particular science. Second, it restricts jadal to a dialogue between two people, whereas one can engage in jadal alone by anticipating an opponent's objections and responding to them, as legal theorists do in their writings. This critique highlights the view that jadal can be a solitary intellectual exercise, not limited to face-to-face debate.

تردد الكلام

Key Takeaway
Al-Baji's definition of jadal fails because it is simultaneously too broad (applies to all fields) and too narrow (requires two participants), missing the solitary dialectical practice common in usul al-fiqh.

Critique of Defining Jadal as Repelling with Proof or Doubt
Al-Juwayni critiques the definition of jadal as repelling the opponent with a proof or a doubt.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify why the definition 'repelling the opponent with a proof or a doubt' is insufficient and reconstruct al-Juwayni's counterexample.

Core Idea
Jadal is defined by mutual engagement, not by the act of repelling.

Definitions of jadal (dialectical disputation) often focus on the outward act of repelling an opponent. Al-Juwayni here exposes a flaw in one such definition: it fails to account for cases where a disputant is silenced without actively repelling, or where repelling does not create a genuine disputation. Understanding this critique sharpens your grasp of what makes an exchange truly dialectical.

Guided Path
1
Identify the proposed definition
Locate the definition that al-Juwayni is critiquing: 'repelling the opponent with a proof or a doubt' (دفع الخصم بحجة أو شبهة). This definition equates jadal with the act of driving back the adversary using either certain proof (حجة) or a doubtful argument (شبهة).
The definition is attributed to 'some later scholars' and specifically to Ali ibn Hamza.
2
Extract al-Juwayni's objection
Al-Juwayni states 'This is an error' (وهذا خطأ). Find his two counterexamples: (1) a person who is silenced (ينقطع) in conversation is still a disputant, even without repelling; (2) one who initiates repelling may cause silence, but the repeller is not necessarily engaged in jadal, nor is the silenced opponent a disputant of the repeller.
The key Arabic terms: ينقطع (is silenced) and دفع (repelling).
3
Understand the logic of the counterexample
Al-Juwayni's argument shows that the definition is both too broad and too narrow. It excludes someone who is silenced without repelling (they are still a disputant), and it includes cases where repelling occurs but no genuine mutual disputation exists. Thus the act of repelling is neither necessary nor sufficient for jadal.
This is a common logical move: test necessity and sufficiency.
4
Articulate the correct concept of jadal
From the critique, infer that jadal requires a reciprocal engagement, not just one-sided repelling. The definition fails because it focuses on an external effect (repelling) rather than the interactive process between two disputants.
Later scholars like al-Taftazani emphasize the structured exchange of objections and responses.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فذهب بعض المتأخرين إلى أن حده هو دفع الخصم بحجة أو شبهة، وبه قال علي بن حمزة (4). وهذا خطأ، فإن من ينقطع في مكالمة خصمه كان مناظرا، وإن لم يدفع خصمه بحجة أو شبهة، وقد تبتدئ الخصم بحجة أو شبهة فيسكت وينقطع من تريد مناظرته، فلم يكن الدفع له مناظرة ولا المدفوع مناظرا للدافع .
Some later scholars held that its definition is repelling the opponent with a proof or a doubt, and Ali ibn Hamza held this. This is an error, because the one who is silenced in conversation with his opponent is a disputant, even if he did not repel his opponent with a proof or a doubt; and you might begin repelling the opponent with a proof or a doubt, and he remains silent and is silenced—the one you intend to dispute with—so repelling him is not disputation, nor is the repelled one a disputant of the repeller.
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage records a definition of jadal as 'repelling the opponent with a proof or a doubt,' attributed to some later scholars and specifically to Ali ibn Hamza. Al-Juwayni criticizes this definition as erroneous. He argues that a person who is silenced during discussion (munqati') is still considered a disputant (munazir), even if he did not actively repel his opponent. Conversely, if someone initiates a repelling argument and the opponent falls silent, the repeller is not necessarily engaged in a mutual disputation, and the silenced opponent is not a disputant relative to the repeller. Thus the definition incorrectly focuses on the act of repelling rather than the interactive nature of jadal.

Key Terms
دفع الخصم بحجة أو شبهة
ينقطع
مناظرا
مناظرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because it includes both proof and doubt
B) Because a person can be a disputant without actively repelling
C) Because it requires two persons
D) Because it is too specific

Key Takeaway
To define jadal, one must focus on the reciprocal structure of disputation, not on the unilateral act of repelling the opponent.
